<p><b>Anguilla</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/ŋ/ 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>ang-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">GWIL</span></span></b>-ə</i></a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British overseas territory</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Introduction_::Anguilla_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Introduction_::Anguilla-3">[3]</a></sup> It is one of the most northerly of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, lying east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a> and directly north of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>. The territory consists of the main island of Anguilla, approximately 16 miles (26 km) long by 3 miles (5 km) wide at its widest point, together with a number of much smaller islands and <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a> with no permanent population. The island's capital is <a href="/wiki/The_Valley,_Anguilla" title="The Valley, Anguilla">The Valley</a>. The total land area of the territory is 35 square miles (90 km<sup>2</sup>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-facts-4">[4]</a></sup> with a population of approximately 13,500 (2006 estimate).</p>
<p>Anguilla has become a popular <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>, having no capital gains, estate, profit or other forms of direct taxation on either individuals or corporations. In April 2011, faced with a mounting deficit, it introduced a 3% "Interim Stabilisation Levy", Anguilla's first form of <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Etymology"></span></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name Anguilla is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicization_of_names" title="Anglicization of names">anglicised</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latinization_of_names" title="Latinization of names">latinate</a> form of earlier Spanish <i><span lang="es" xml:lang="es">anguila</span></i>, French <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">anguille</span></i>, or Italian <i><span lang="it" xml:lang="it">anguilla</span></i>, all meaning "<a href="/wiki/Eel" title="Eel">eel</a>" in reference to the island's shape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1839_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1839-6">[6]</a></sup> For similar reasons, it was formerly known as <b>Snake</b> or <b>Snake Island</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1839_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1839-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1911_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1911-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Anguilla" title="History of Anguilla">History of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wallblake_House,_The_Valley.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="2048" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg/220px-Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg/330px-Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg/440px-Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wallblake_House,_The_Valley.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wallblake_House" title="Wallblake House">Wallblake House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Anguilla was first settled by Indigenous Amerindian peoples who migrated from South America. The earliest Native American artefacts found on Anguilla have been dated to around 1300 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>; remains of settlements date from <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span> 600.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> name for the island seems to have been <b>Malliouhana</b>. The date of European colonisation is uncertain: some sources claim that <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a> sighted the island during his second voyage in 1493, while others state that the island's first European explorer was the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a> Huguenot nobleman and merchant mariner <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Goulaine_de_Laudonni%C3%A8re" title="René Goulaine de Laudonnière">René Goulaine de Laudonnière</a> in 1564.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-gov-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traditional accounts state that Anguilla was first colonised by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> settlers from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> beginning in 1650.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1839_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1839-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In this early colonial period, however, Anguilla sometimes served as a place of refuge and recent scholarship focused on Anguilla has placed greater significance on other Europeans and <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">creoles</a> migrating from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Kitts" title="St. Kitts">St. Christopher</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. The French temporarily took over the island in 1666 but returned it to English control under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breda_(1667)" title="Treaty of Breda (1667)">Treaty of Breda</a> the next year. A Major John Scott who visited in September 1667, wrote of leaving the island "in good condition" and noted that in July 1668, "200 or 300 people fled thither in time of war".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is likely that some of these early Europeans brought enslaved Africans with them. Historians confirm that <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> lived in the region in the early 17th century. For example, Africans from <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> lived in St. Christopher in 1626. By 1672 a slave depot existed on the island of Nevis, serving the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>. While the time of African arrival in Anguilla is difficult to place precisely, archival evidence indicates a substantial African presence of at least 100 slaves by 1683. These seem to have come from Central Africa as well as West Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walicek.2C_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Walicek.2C_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Attempts by the French to capture the island during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Austrian_Succession" title="War of Austrian Succession">War of Austrian Succession</a> (<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Anguilla" title="Battle of Anguilla">1745</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> (1796) ended in failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-gov-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the early colonial period, Anguilla was administered by the British through Antigua; in 1825, it was placed under the administrative control of nearby Saint Kitts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-gov-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1967, Britain granted Saint Kitts and <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> full internal autonomy. Anguilla was also incorporated into the new unified dependency, named <a href="/wiki/Saint_Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla" title="Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla">Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla</a>, against the wishes of many Anguillians. This led to two Anguillian Revolutions in 1967 and 1969 headed by Atlin Harrigan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Webster" title="Ronald Webster">Ronald Webster</a>. The island briefly operated as the independent "<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Anguilla" title="Republic of Anguilla">Republic of Anguilla</a>". The goal of the revolution was not independence per se, but rather independence from Saint Kitts and Nevis and a return to being a British colony. British authority was fully restored in July 1971 and in 1980 Anguilla was finally allowed to secede from Saint Kitts and Nevis and become a separate British <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a> (now a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Introduction_::Anguilla_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Introduction_::Anguilla-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1358" data-file-width="2206" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the European Union in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">Political system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Anguilla" title="Politics of Anguilla">Politics of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Anguilla" title="Law of Anguilla">Law of Anguilla</a></div>
<p>Anguilla is an internally self-governing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">overseas territory</a> of the United Kingdom. Its politics take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependency</a>, whereby the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister" title="Chief Minister">Chief Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pluriform" title="wikt:pluriform">pluriform</a> multi-party system.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="United Nations Committee on Decolonization">United Nations Committee on Decolonization</a> includes Anguilla on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories</a>. The territory's constitution is Anguilla Constitutional Order 1 April 1982 (amended 1990). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anguilla_House_of_Assembly" title="Anguilla House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature.</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence">Defence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Defence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a dependency of the UK, the UK is responsible for Anguilla's military defence, although there are no active <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garrisons" title="Garrisons">garrisons</a> or armed forces present. Anguilla has a small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_police" title="Marine police">marine police</a> force, comprising around 32 personnel, which operates one M160-class fast <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol boat</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Anguilla" title="Demographics of Anguilla">Demographics of Anguilla</a></div>
<p>The majority of residents (90.08%) are black, the descendants of slaves transported from Africa. Minorities include whites at 3.74% and people of mixed race at 4.65% (figures from 2001 census).</p>
<p>72% of the population is Anguillian while 28% is non-Anguillian (2001 census). Of the non-Anguillian population, many are citizens of the United States, United Kingdom, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Kitts_%26_Nevis" title="St Kitts &amp; Nevis">St Kitts &amp; Nevis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.</p>
<p>2006 and 2007 saw an influx of large numbers of Chinese, Indian and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_people" title="Mexican people">Mexican</a> workers, brought in as labour for major tourist developments due to the local population not being large enough to support the labour requirements.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Christian churches did not have a consistent or strong presence during the initial period of English colonisation. Spiritual and religious practices of Europeans and Africans tended to reflect their regional origins. As early as 1813, Christian ministers formally ministered to enslaved Africans and promoted literacy among converts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wesleyan" title="Wesleyan">Wesleyan</a> (Methodist) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Missionary_Society_of_England" title="Missionary Society of England">Missionary Society of England</a> built churches and schools in 1817.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2001 census, Christianity is Anguilla's predominant religion, with 29 percent of the population practising <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>. Another 23.9 percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist">Methodist</a>. Other churches on the island include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (served by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Saint_John%27s_-_Basseterre" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Saint John's - Basseterre">Roman Catholic Diocese of Saint John's - Basseterre</a>, with see at Saint John on <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>) and a community of <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.7%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statistics_census_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-statistics_census-18">[18]</a></sup> Between 1992 and 2001 the number of followers of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Cleveland,_Tennessee)" title="Church of God (Cleveland, Tennessee)">Church of God</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostals" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> increased considerably. There are at least 15 churches on the island. Although a minority on the island, it is an important location to followers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafarian</a> religion – Anguilla is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Athlyi_Rogers" title="Robert Athlyi Rogers">Robert Athlyi Rogers</a>, author of <a href="/wiki/Holy_Piby" title="Holy Piby">The Holy Piby</a> which has had a strong influence on Rastafarian beliefs. Various other religions are practised as well. More recently a Muslim cultural center has opened on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statistics_census_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-statistics_census-18">[18]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anguillian_Creole" title="Anguillian Creole">Anguillian Creole</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="620" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg/220px-Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg/330px-Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg/440px-Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Overlooking <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Ground,_Anguilla" title="Sandy Ground, Anguilla">Sandy Ground</a>, Anguilla</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Today most people in Anguilla speak a British-influenced variety of standard English. Other languages are also spoken on the island, including varieties of Spanish, Chinese and the languages of other immigrants. However, the most common language other than Standard English is the island's own English-lexifier Creole language (not to be confused with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">Antillean Creole</a> ('French Creole'), spoken in French islands such as <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>). It is referred to locally by terms such as "dialect" (pronounced "dialek"), Anguilla Talk or "Anguillian". It has its main roots in early varieties of English and West African languages, and is similar to the dialects spoken in English-speaking islands throughout the Eastern Caribbean, in terms of its structural features and to the extent of being considered one single language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Linguists who are interested in the origins of Anguillian and other Caribbean Creoles point out that some of its grammatical features can be traced to African languages while others can be traced to European languages. Three areas have been identified as significant for the identification of the linguistic origins of those forced migrants who arrived before 1710: the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region)" title="Gold Coast (region)">Gold Coast</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Coast" title="Slave Coast">Slave Coast</a> and the Windward Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sociohistorical information from Anguilla's archives suggest that Africans and Europeans formed two distinct, but perhaps overlapping speech communities in the early phases of the island's colonisation. "Anguillian" is believed to have emerged as the language of the masses as time passed, slavery was abolished and locals began to see themselves as "belonging" to Anguillian society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walicek.2C_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Walicek.2C_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg/220px-Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg/330px-Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg/440px-Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The beach at the Cap Juluca resort on Maundays Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg/220px-Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg/330px-Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg/440px-Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anguilla-Island_Harbour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Island Harbour</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla_National_Trust&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anguilla National Trust (page does not exist)">Anguilla National Trust</a> (ANT) was established in 1988 and opened its offices in 1993 charged with the responsibility of preserving the heritage of the island, including its cultural heritage. The Trust has programmes encouraging Anguillian writers and the preservation of the island's history. In 2015, <i>Where I See The Sun – Contemporary Poetry in Anguilla</i> A New Anthology by <a href="/wiki/Lasana_M._Sekou" title="Lasana M. Sekou">Lasana M. Sekou</a> was published by House of Nehesi Publishers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Among the forty three poets in the unprecedented collection are Rita Celestine-Carty, <a href="/wiki/Bankie_Banx" title="Bankie Banx">Bankie Banx</a>, John T. Harrigan, Patricia J. Adams, Fabian Fahie, Dr. Oluwakemi Linda Banks, and Reuel Ben Lewi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The island's cultural history begins with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Taíno people">Taino</a> Native Americans. Artifacts have been found around the island, telling of life before European settlers arrived by the <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Carib</a> peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>As throughout the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, holidays are a cultural fixture. Anguilla's most important holidays are of historic as much as cultural importance – particularly the anniversary of the emancipation (previously August Monday in the Park), celebrated as the Summer Festival. British festivities, such as the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Official_Birthday" title="Queen's Official Birthday">Queen's Birthday</a>, are also celebrated.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anguillian_cuisine" title="Anguillian cuisine">Anguillian cuisine</a></div>
<p>Anguillian cuisine is influenced by native Caribbean, African, Spanish, French and English cuisines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup> Seafood is abundant, including prawns, shrimp, crab, <a href="/wiki/Spiny_lobster" title="Spiny lobster">spiny lobster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conch" title="Conch">conch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahi-mahi" title="Mahi-mahi">mahi-mahi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutjanus_campechanus" title="Lutjanus campechanus">red snapper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">grouper</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_cod" title="Salt cod">Salt cod</a> is a staple food eaten by itself and used in stews, casseroles and soups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup> Livestock is limited due to the small size of the island and people there utilise poultry, pork, goat and mutton, along with imported beef.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup> Goat is the most commonly eaten meat, utilised in a variety of dishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>A significant amount of the island's produce is imported due to limited land suitable for agriculture production; much of the soil is sandy and infertile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-5"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup> Among the agriculture produced in Anguilla includes tomatoes, <a href="/wiki/Bell_pepper" title="Bell pepper">peppers</a>, limes and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citrus_fruit" title="Citrus fruit">citrus fruits</a>, onion, garlic, squash, <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon peas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a>. Starch staple foods include imported rice and other foods that are imported or locally grown, including <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewYorkTimes_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewYorkTimes-25">[25]</a></sup> sweet potatoes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewYorkTimes_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-NewYorkTimes-25">[25]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UsaToday_24-6"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to its internationally recognised culinary community, the island has enjoyed a reputation as "the culinary capital of the Caribbean". This reputation was reinforced with the publication of the <i><b>(WE) Are Anguilla Cookbook</b></i>, a guide to the cuisine of Anguilla featuring emerging and established local chefs, who share both their signature dishes and personal anecdotes regarding the island's epicurean culture. A publishing contract was secured by The Britto Agency, which had conceived the idea for the book itself.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Anguilla" title="Music of Anguilla">Music of Anguilla</a></div>
<p>The island's burgeoning musical community made history with the recording of Sounds of Anguilla (Volume 1), the first album ever composed solely of artists from a single Caribbean island representing multiple musical genres: pop, <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>, hip-hop, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca music</a> and R&amp;B. The production was the brainchild of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marvet_Britto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marvet Britto (page does not exist)">Marvet Britto</a> of the Britto Agency, the island's global public relations and brand-architecture firm. Britto secured a recording contract with Massenburg and both served as executive producers along with Haydn Hughes, at that time the Parliamentary Secretary Responsible for Tourism. Sounds of Anguilla (Volume 1) debuted on iTunes on 30 June 2015 and included celebrated Anguillian musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Bankie_Banx" title="Bankie Banx">Bankie Banx</a>, Amalia Watty, True Intentions and Gerswin Lake and The Parables.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Anguilla" title="Education in Anguilla">Education in Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Anguilla" title="List of schools in Anguilla">List of schools in Anguilla</a></div>
<p>A branch of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_James_School_of_Medicine" title="Saint James School of Medicine">Saint James School of Medicine</a> was established in 2011 in Anguilla.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/For-profit_school" title="For-profit school">for-profit</a> medical school headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Park_Ridge,_Illinois" title="Park Ridge, Illinois">Park Ridge, Illinois</a>. The school's mission is to help motivated students become a doctor, irrespective of ethnic, religious and cultural backgrounds. The school was founded on the belief that a high quality medical education should be affordable and accessible to everyone with the commitment and the ability to succeed in a career in medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="243" data-file-width="324" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg/220px-Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Square_rigger" title="Square rigger">square rigger</a> viewed from Long Bay</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sailing_in_Anguilla" title="Sailing in Anguilla">Sailing in Anguilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Anguilla" title="Rugby union in Anguilla">Rugby union in Anguilla</a></div>
<p>Boat racing has deep roots in Anguillian culture and is the national sport.</p>
<p>There are regular sailing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regattas" title="Regattas">regattas</a> on national holidays, such as Carnival, which are contested by locally built and designed boats. These boats have names and have sponsors that print their logo on their sails.</p>
<p>As in many other former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Colony" title="British Colony">British colonies</a>, cricket is also a popular sport. Anguilla is the home of <a href="/wiki/Omari_Banks" title="Omari Banks">Omari Banks</a>, who played for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indies_Cricket_Team" title="West Indies Cricket Team">West Indies Cricket Team</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Cardigan_Connor" title="Cardigan Connor">Cardigan Connor</a> played first-class cricket for English county side <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Hampshire County Cricket Club">Hampshire</a> and was 'chef de mission' (team manager) for Anguilla's <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> team in 2002.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is represented in Anguilla by the Anguilla Eels RFC, who were formed in April 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The Eels have been finalists in the St. Martin tournament in November 2006 and semi-finalists in 2007, 2008, 2009 and Champions in 2010. The Eels were formed in 2006 by Scottish club national second row Martin Welsh, Club Sponsor and President of the AERFC Ms. Jacquie Ruan, and Canadian standout Scrumhalf Mark Harris (Toronto Scottish RFC).</p>
<p>Anguilla is also the birthplace of sprinter <a href="/wiki/Zharnel_Hughes" title="Zharnel Hughes">Zharnel Hughes</a> who represents Great Britain since 2015. He specialises in the 100m and 200m sprints. He won the 100m in the <a href="/wiki/2013_CARIFTA_Games" title="2013 CARIFTA Games">2013 CARIFTA Games</a> with a time of 10.44 seconds, despite his time being some way below his personal best.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> He currently holds the ISSA/GraceKennedy Boys' and Girls' Athletics Championships record for the 100m, with a time of 10.12 seconds having taken the record from Yohan Blake.[5][6] On 13 March 2015, Hughes made his Diamond League debut where he was commended for almost beating world champion Usain Bolt.[7] On 24 July 2015, Hughes won the 200m at the London Diamond League meet to take the lead in the Diamond League standings for the season.[8] On 27 August 2015, Hughes came 5th in the 200m at the World Championships in Beijing with a time of 20.02 seconds.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shara_Proctor" title="Shara Proctor">Shara Proctor</a>, British Long Jump Silver Medalist in World Championships in Beijing first represented Anguilla in the event until 2010 when she began to represent the UK. Under the Anguillian Flag she achieved several medals in the <a href="/wiki/North_American,_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Athletic_Association" title="North American, Central American and Caribbean Athletic Association">NACAC</a> games.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Keith_Connor" title="Keith Connor">Keith Connor</a>, triple jumper, is also an Anguillian. He represented Great Britain and achieved several international titles including Commonwealth and European Games gold medals and an Olympic bronze medal. Keith later became Head Coach of Australia Athletics. <a href="/wiki/Chesney_Hughes" title="Chesney Hughes">Chesney Hughes</a>, is a West Indian cricketer who plays for Derbyshire. He was born in Anguilla. Having signed for the side in June 2009, and holding a British passport, Hughes made his List A debut for the side during the 2009 Pro40 League against Warwickshire.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_history">Natural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Natural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Anguilla has habitat for the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_tree_frog" title="Cuban tree frog">Cuban tree frogs</a> (<i>Osteopilus septentrionalis</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Townsend_et_al._2000_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Townsend_et_al._2000-30">[30]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Red-footed_tortoise" title="Red-footed tortoise">red-footed tortoise</a> (<i>Chelonoidis carbonaria</i>) is a species of tortoise found here, it somehow came from South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-23">[23]</a></sup> Hurricanes led to over-water dispersal for the <a href="/wiki/Green_iguana" title="Green iguana">green iguanas</a> (<i>Iguana iguana</i>) to colonise Anguilla.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Censky_et_al._1998_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Censky_et_al._1998-31">[31]</a></sup> All three amphibians are introduced (though tortoises and iguanas are generally introduced as reptiles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Five species of bats are known in the literature from Anguilla — the threatened <a href="/wiki/Insular_single_leaf_bat" title="Insular single leaf bat">insular single leaf bat</a> (<i>Monophyllus plethodon</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Antillean_fruit-eating_bat" title="Antillean fruit-eating bat">Antillean fruit-eating bat</a> (<i>Brachyphylla cavernarum</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_fruit_bat" title="Jamaican fruit bat">Jamaican fruit bat</a> (<i>Artibeus jamaicensis</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_funnel-eared_bat" title="Mexican funnel-eared bat">Mexican funnel-eared bat</a> (<i>Natalus stramineus</i>), and the <a href="/wiki/Velvety_free-tailed_bat" title="Velvety free-tailed bat">velvety free-tailed bat</a> (<i>Molossus molossus</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genoways_et_al.n2007_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Genoways_et_al.n2007-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Anguilla" title="Geography of Anguilla">Geography of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3672" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg/220px-Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg/330px-Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg/440px-Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An aerial view of the western portion of the island of Anguilla. The Blowing Point ferry terminal is visible in the lower right, as are (right to left) Shaddick Point, Rendezvous Bay, Cove Bay and Maundays Bay.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Anguilla is a flat, low-lying island of <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a>. It is directly north of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, separated from that island by the <a href="/wiki/Anguilla_Channel" title="Anguilla Channel">Anguilla Channel</a>. The soil is generally thin and poor, supporting scrub, tropical and forest vegetation.</p>
<p>Anguilla is noted for its spectacular and ecologically important <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and beaches. Apart from the main island of Anguilla itself, the territory includes a number of other smaller islands and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cays" title="Cays">cays</a>, mostly tiny and uninhabited. Some of these are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anguillita" title="Anguillita">Anguillita</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dog_Island,_Anguilla" title="Dog Island, Anguilla">Dog Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prickly_Pear_Cays" title="Prickly Pear Cays">Prickly Pear Cays</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Island,_Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sandy Island, Anguilla (page does not exist)">Sandy Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scrub_Island,_Anguilla" title="Scrub Island, Anguilla">Scrub Island</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Scilly_Cay,_Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Scilly Cay, Anguilla (page does not exist)">Scilly Cay</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seal_Island,_Anguilla" title="Seal Island, Anguilla">Seal Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sombrero,_Anguilla" title="Sombrero, Anguilla">Sombrero</a>, also known as Hat Island</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Anguilla has a volcanic origin<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRINCETON_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRINCETON-33">[33]</a></sup> and has been submerged repeatedly from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<table>
<tr valign="top">
<td>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SSS_Islands_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="527" height="386" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/SSS_Islands_Map.png/300px-SSS_Islands_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/SSS_Islands_Map.png/450px-SSS_Islands_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/SSS_Islands_Map.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SSS_Islands_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

</div>
</div>
</td>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anguilla_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="328" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Anguilla_map.png/250px-Anguilla_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/Anguilla_map.png 1.5x" width="250"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Anguilla" title="Climate of Anguilla">Climate of Anguilla</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature">Temperature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Temperature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Northeastern trade winds keep this tropical island relatively cool and dry. Average annual temperature is 80 °F (27 °C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-facts-4">[4]</a></sup> July–October is its hottest period, December–February, its coolest.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rainfall">Rainfall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rainfall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rainfall averages 35 inches (890 mm) annually,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-facts-4">[4]</a></sup> although the figures vary from season to season and year to year. The island is subject to both sudden tropical storms and hurricanes, which occur in the period from July to November. The island suffered damage in 1995 from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> and severe flooding 5–20 feet from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Anguilla" title="Economy of Anguilla">Economy of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="810" data-file-width="1033" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg/300px-Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg/450px-Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg/600px-Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2009 export percentages</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Anguilla's thin arid soil being largely unsuitable for agriculture, the island has few land-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_resources" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a>. Its main industries are tourism, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Offshore_companies" title="Offshore companies">offshore incorporation and management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Offshore_bank" title="Offshore bank">offshore banking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Captive_insurance" title="Captive insurance">captive insurance</a> and fishing.</p>
<p>Before the 2008 worldwide crisis the economy of Anguilla was expanding rapidly, especially the tourism sector which was driving major new developments in partnerships with multi-national companies.</p>
<p>Anguilla's currency is the <a href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_dollar" title="East Caribbean dollar">East Caribbean dollar</a>, though the US dollar is also widely accepted. The exchange rate is fixed to the US dollar at US$1 = EC$2.70.</p>
<p>The economy, and especially the tourism sector, suffered a setback in late 1995 due to the effects of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> in September but recovered in 1996. Hotels were hit particularly hard during this time. Another economic setback occurred during the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a> in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anguilla's financial system comprises 7 banks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> 2 money services businesses, more than 40 company managers, more than 50 insurers, 12 brokers, more than 250 captive intermediaries, more than 50 mutual funds and 8 trust companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anguilla's tourism industry received a major boost when it was selected to host the <a href="/wiki/World_Travel_Awards" title="World Travel Awards">World Travel Awards</a> in December 2014. Known as "the Oscars of the travel industry", the awards ceremony was held at the <a href="/wiki/CuisinArt_Resort_and_Spa" title="CuisinArt Resort and Spa">CuisinArt Resort and Spa</a> and was hosted by award-winning actress <a href="/wiki/Vivica_A._Fox" title="Vivica A. Fox">Vivica A. Fox</a>. Anguilla was voted the <b>World's Leading Luxury Island Destination</b> from a short list of top-tier candidates such as St. Barts, Maldives and Mauritius. The event marked a first in the island's history and was arranged and organised by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marvet_Britto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marvet Britto (page does not exist)">Marvet Britto</a> of the Britto Agency, which oversees Global Brand Strategy and Public Relations for the island.</p>
<p>Anguilla aims to obtain 15% of its energy from <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> so it is less reliant on expensive imported diesel. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a> is helping the government gather the information it needs to change the territory's legislation, so it can integrate renewables into its grid. <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, have also made good progress in switching to renewables, but many other SIDS are still at the early stages of planning how to integrate renewable energy into their grids. "For a small island we're very far ahead," said Beth Barry, Coordinator of the Anguilla Renewable Energy Office. "We've got an Energy Policy and a draft Climate Change policy and have been focussing efforts on the question of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> supply for several years now. As a result we have a lot of information we can share with other islands."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Anguilla" title="Transport in Anguilla">Transport in Anguilla</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Anguilla is served by <a href="/wiki/Clayton_J._Lloyd_International_Airport" title="Clayton J. Lloyd International Airport">Clayton J. Lloyd International Airport</a> (prior to 4 July 2010 known as Wallblake Airport). The primary runway at the airport is 5,462 feet (1,665 m) in length and can accommodate moderate-sized aircraft. Services connect to various other Caribbean islands via regional carrier <a href="/wiki/LIAT" title="LIAT">LIAT</a>, local charter airlines and others. Although there are no direct scheduled flights to or from continental America or Europe, <a href="/wiki/Tradewind_Aviation" title="Tradewind Aviation">Tradewind Aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a> provide scheduled air service to San Juan, Puerto Rico. The airport can handle large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narrow-body" title="Narrow-body">narrow-body</a> jets such as the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aside from taxis, there is no public transport on the island. Cars drive on the left.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boat">Boat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Boat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are regular ferries from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> to Anguilla. It is a 20-minute crossing from <a href="/wiki/Marigot,_Saint_Martin" title="Marigot, Saint Martin">Marigot</a>, St. Martin to Blowing Point, Anguilla. Ferries commence service from 7:00 am. There is also a Charter Service, from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blowing_Point" title="Blowing Point">Blowing Point</a>, Anguilla to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Juliana_Airport" title="Princess Juliana Airport">Princess Juliana Airport</a> to make travel easier. This way of travel is the most common method of transport between Anguilla and St. Martin or St. Maarten.</p>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
<div>
<ul>
<li>1. <a href="/wiki/Condominium" title="Condominium">Occupied jointly</a> with the United States.</li>
<li>2. In 1931, Canada and other British <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominions</a> obtained self-government through the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>. See <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Canada" title="Name of Canada">Name of Canada</a>.</li>
<li>3. Gave up <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">self-rule</a> in 1934, but remained a <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> Dominion until it <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">joined Canada</a> in 1949.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>6. <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a>.</li>
<li>7. <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">Self-governing</a> Southern Rhodesia <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia%27s_Unilateral_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Rhodesia's Unilateral Declaration of Independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> in 1965 (as <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>) and continued as an <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">unrecognised</a> state until the 1979 <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_House_Agreement" title="Lancaster House Agreement">Lancaster House Agreement</a>. After recognised independence in 1980, Zimbabwe was a member of the Commonwealth until it withdrew in 2003.</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
